actual fun randomUUID() = java.util.UUID.randomUUID().toString()

Ktor for multiplatform HTTP:

// commonMain
val client = HttpClient {
    install(ContentNegotiation) { json() }
}
suspend fun fetchUser(id: String): User =
    client.get("https://api.example.com/users/$id").body()

SQLDelight for multiplatform DB:

-- app/src/commonMain/sqldelight/User.sq
CREATE TABLE User (id TEXT NOT NULL PRIMARY KEY, name TEXT NOT NULL);
selectAll: SELECT * FROM User;
insert: INSERT OR REPLACE INTO User VALUES ?;
// Generated type-safe Kotlin queries (works on Android + iOS)
val users: List<User> = queries.selectAll().executeAsList()
Q.When to choose React Native vs Flutter vs KMP vs Native
🔥
+

The honest decision framework for 2026:

  • Pure native Android — performance-critical features (camera, video, AR), or you only ship Android. Compose + Kotlin is the gold standard. Always available as a fallback.
  • KMP — Kotlin/Android team wanting iOS too; share business logic without giving up native UI; incremental adoption in existing apps; best for teams where Android is primary.
  • Flutter — design-system-heavy apps needing pixel-perfect custom UI across platforms; single Dart codebase; stronger when web output also needed; best for teams starting fresh with no mobile codebase.
  • React Native — web (React/TS) team expanding to mobile; tightest web↔mobile code reuse; brownfield gradual migration; large npm ecosystem. New arch closes the performance gap.
SignalBest choice
"We have Kotlin engineers, want iOS"KMP
"We have a React web team"React Native
"We need custom pixel-perfect UI everywhere"Flutter
"One platform, max performance"Native
"Gradual migration from old app"RN (brownfield) or KMP (add iOS layer)
Q.How does the React Native JS bridge actually work? (old arch internals)
+

Three threads, async message passing:

  1. JS Thread — runs your JS/TS code in the Hermes engine
  2. Shadow Thread — yoga-based layout engine computes layout from JS Flexbox specs
  3. Main Thread — renders native views from computed layout

A button press → native module call flow:

  1. User taps → event from Main Thread → serialized JSON → bridge → JS Thread
  2. JS event handler runs → calls NativeModules.GPS.getCurrentLocation()
  3. Serialized JSON call → bridge → Main Thread → native GPS API
  4. GPS result → serialized JSON → bridge → JS Thread → callback/promise resolves

The bottleneck: every cross-thread call serializes to JSON strings. Large objects (images, video frames) are expensive. The bridge is single-threaded — a backlog here drops frames.

New Architecture (JSI) fix: JS holds a C++ reference to the native object. Calls are synchronous and zero-copy. No serialization. The bridge is gone.

Q.KMP vs full-native per platform — what do you share, what stays native?
+
LayerShare in KMP?Notes
Data models / DTOs✅ YesPure Kotlin data classes
Networking (Ktor)✅ YesHTTP client, serialization
Business logic / use cases✅ YesNo platform dependencies
Caching / DB (SQLDelight)✅ YesSQL is platform-neutral
ViewModel / state⚠️ PartialKMP ViewModel (lifecycle-aware) in 2024+
UI⚠️ OptionalCompose Multiplatform shares; or native SwiftUI/Compose
Platform APIs❌ via expect/actualCamera, Bluetooth, sensors — platform-specific

Airbnb approach (2025): ~95% code share — shared everything down to individual composables where Compose Multiplatform supports it. iOS gets Compose MP for most screens; SwiftUI only for deeply native interactions (camera, share sheet).

Q.Compose Multiplatform vs native UI per platform
+

Compose Multiplatform (by JetBrains) — Compose UI targeting Android, iOS, Desktop, Web from one codebase.

iOS production stable since late 2024. Used by Netflix, Airbnb, Cash App in production.

Compose MultiplatformNative (Compose + SwiftUI)
Code share~95% including UI~50-70% (logic only)
Native feelVery close; not pixel-perfect system controlsPerfect — uses system widgets
Custom UIExcellentSame effort per platform
Platform integrationVia expect/actualDirect
iOS engineer required?MinimalYes, for SwiftUI screens
Recommendation for 2026: if your app's UI is custom (not relying on system controls like UIDatePicker, UIDocumentPicker, etc.), Compose Multiplatform is production-viable and dramatically reduces iOS development cost for Android teams.
Q.Practical RN project structure for Android engineers joining a RN team
+
my-app/
├── android/              ← Android project (open in AS for native work)
├── ios/                  ← iOS project
├── src/
│   ├── screens/          ← Top-level screen components (HomeScreen.tsx)
│   ├── components/       ← Reusable UI components
│   ├── navigation/       ← Navigator setup, route types
│   ├── store/            ← State management (Zustand/Redux)
│   ├── api/              ← API client, network layer
│   ├── hooks/            ← Custom hooks (useAuth, useDebounce)
│   ├── utils/            ← Pure utility functions
│   ├── types/            ← TypeScript interfaces
│   └── native/           ← Native module wrappers + TypeScript API
│       ├── bluetooth/
│       │   ├── BluetoothModule.kt    ← Android implementation
│       │   ├── BluetoothModule.ts    ← JS wrapper
│       │   └── index.ts              ← Clean public API
├── __tests__/
├── index.js              ← Entry point (registers App component)
├── metro.config.js       ← Bundler config
└── package.json
Android engineers: the android/ folder is a real Android project. Open it in Android Studio to write native modules. The rest is JS/TS territory — treat src/ like your Kotlin source tree, just in TypeScript.
